A lot of GOP politicians and political pundits are blaming Biden for this inflation THEY ARE LYING TO YOU n n If Biden s spending is causing this inflation why didn t we see inflation rise in when Trump spent EVEN MORE money n n Why did inflation not spike back in March when Biden s only stimulus went out n n Why did inflation rise AFTER the Federal Unemployment benefit was eliminated completely in September And it was already reduced from per week when Trump was president down to per week when Biden took office n n How could Biden s spending with his Infrastructure Bill cause inflation BEFORE any money from it was spent n n Why would inflation rise after Biden REDUCED THE DEFICIT and spent LESS money than Trump n nThe TRUTH is that Biden s spending is NOT THE CAUSE OF THIS INFLATION n nSo what is causing this inflation n nThere are several factors that are causing today s inflation n n When the pandemic hit in we went into lock down Restaurants closed People stopped spending money Demand dropped Manufacturers drastically slowed or even stopped manufacturing part in response to the reduced demand and part in response to the lack of labor due to the people getting Covid and or being quarantined n n When the lock downs ended and people started going back out earlier this year they not only went back to spending money they made up for lost time This created a huge and sudden increase in demand n n Unfortunately increasing supplies is not that simple Our supplier chain is made up of millions of products from all around the globe and many of our larger more complex items have to be manufactured from other parts in the global chain and these manufacturers can t up their output until their suppliers up theirs It s not just the manufacturers that have to ramp back up it s shipping companies trucking companies retailers and everybody in between n n Inflation increases the costs of doing business which in a free market should cause a reduction in corporate profits Yet many large companies showed RECORD PROFITS this year This is because in several large industries there are only a handful of competitors which allows them to raise prices above what a free market would allow and they have used the pandemic and supply chain issues as an excuse to do exactly that n nThe bottom line is that Demand was able to increase much faster than supply THAT along with the corporate manipulation of prices IS WHAT IS DRIVING THIS INFLATION n nP S Let s remember that the President does not control inflation Our economy is based on a free market Absent extreme circumstances he cannot order companies to raise or lower prices or to keep them the same He certainly cannot dictate to foreign companies what they can charge n n

According to renowned political economist Raj Patel rajpateluk and physician and activist Rupa Marya rupa marya our bodies our societies and our planet are inflamed From the Covid pandemic and the shocking racial disparities in its impact to the international response to systemic racism and the backlash from it as well as climate change and the refugees that result from the changes to our planet our bodies are responding to it all through various forms of inflammation n nInflammation is deeply connected to everything the food we eat the air we breathe and the diversity of the microbes living inside us regulating everything from our brain s development to our immune system s functioning It is connected to the traumatic events we experienced as children as well as the traumas endured by our ancestors It can also be the result of access or lack thereof to healthcare and the very models of healthcare that physicians practice n nIn their recent book Inflamed Raj and Rupa reveal the links between health and structural injustices and offer a new deep medicine that can heal our bodies and our world n nJoin Raj and Rupa for a rich unique conversation with professor Charlotte Mar a S enz as they illuminate the hidden relationships between our biological systems and the profound injustices of our political and economic systems Explore the deep medicine of decolonization and its potential to heal not just our bodies but the world n nRegister for this free live online conversation at the linktree in our bio n n deepmedicine inflamed decolonization inflamedbook rajpatel rupamarya ciissf ciissffaculty ciispublicprograms ciispubprograms conversation medicine health healthcare caretakers injustice unjusthealthcare

There is no such a thing as finished reform That s one of the reasons why high income countries continuously reform their healthcare systems The countries are in globalized word connected and they tend to inspire each other and similar reforms are often introduced across countries However politicians are keen to get inspired by other countries in a limited way Recent paper offers overview of health reform trends in high income countries before the covid pandemic n n Even before the pandemic countries were facing challenges which persist today The most important challenges are gaps coverage and access concerns about quality integration and continuity of care workforce shortages the epidemiological shift to multiple chronic diseases emerging viral threats as well as other unpredictable exogenous shocks These are the challenges which lie ahead of us and the competent will be forced to willy nilly to deal with it The question is how they are going to do it n n The average age of the population in most developed countries is growing which means that the demand for healthcare will exponentially grow as well The demand in future will concentrate on person centred care n n In the paper were reviewed reforms which were reported in countries in of them went to four clusters insurance cover age resource generation governance healthcare purchasing payment and organization of hospitalcare n n In reforms in countries were reported of them fell under organization of primary ambulatory care governance care coordination specialized care and organization of hospital care n n Most reforms were reported ongoing in implemented seven abandoned Health agency ledreforms were implemented most frequently followed by central government legislated reforms n n Policymakers can leverage international experience of distinct reform approaches addressing similar challenges and similar approaches to address distinct problems Such knowledge may help inspireor support future successful health reform processes

Erin Palmer for DC Council Chairwoman n nAt a young age I spent a lot of my life moving around and grew up in California and Colorado Later I attended the University of Pennsylvania studied abroad in Santiago Chile and worked in Managua Nicaragua and Quito Ecuador I came to DC to attend American University s law school and graduate school n nAfter completing law school and earning my graduate degree in conflict resolution I worked as a judicial clerk at the DC Court of Appeals where I met my husband Eric who was also clerking at the court We married settled in Takoma DC and had our three kids Adri n Mateo and Javier They are constant and lively reminders of the values we honor most as a family kindness empathy and service to our community n nFrom the start of my professional career I have worked to hold government accountable After my judicial clerkship I worked at a law firm spending most of my time on pro bono matters These included winning asylum for an individual fleeing state violence due to their political beliefs representing a child with disabilities at a local school to ensure they received their needed educational supports and filing briefs with the United States Supreme Court on the science regarding youth brain development to end the use of life without parole sentences for youth n nFor the last seven years I served as an ethics lawyer for the federal judiciary where I specialized in workplace accountability As a survivor of sexual assault and harassment these structural challenges were not just matters of revising rules and procedures but a moral call to redefine safety in our workplaces I m proud of my work to improve accountability and workplace protections within an institution essential to the balance of power in government n nSince I have also served as an Advisory Neighborhood Commissioner a hyper local elected position I ve tackled traffic safety infrastructure housing education and community safety with an eye not just toward fixing the immediate problems but nidentifying systemic challenges and proposing solutions to improve government across DC My trademark as a Commissioner is redefining the role by not solely focusing on the immediate needs in my neighborhood but also building alliances across the District nto make every neighborhood better n nI ve been a leader in a number of community organizations that give back to our city including currently as a Board Member of the Old Takoma Business Association Main Street Takoma Previously I served as Secretary of the Manor Park Citizens Association a Board Member of the Kennedy Street Development Corporation and a Board Member of the Student Education and Leadership Fund which provided college scholarships to DC area students dedicated to using their college education to give back to their local communities

Alan Lowe for Palm Coast City Council District n nHere are some bullet points items of my platform followed by a little more detail n n I oppose tax increases n n I support a fiscally responsible government n n I oppose uncontrolled development n n I support development that does not affect adjacent land values n n I oppose zoning changes that will harm adjacent property values n n I support a healthy business atmosphere n n I support government transparency n n I support ensuring there is a quality and detailed cost benefit analysis performed on all significant projects n n I support public town halls at various locations around town to promote public interaction and comment n n I support a third party forensic budget review to identify areas of wasteful spending n nAs your city councilman I will be a public servant and a community leader that actually listens n nNot only will I bring the expected integrity and transparency back to City Hall I will also bring the truth that all city employees whether elected appointed or hired are servants of the people and that the citizens of Palm Coast deserve their respect in all interactions n nI will fight to restore trust City Council of Palm Coast and make your interests my first priority n nI believe in small government and see the government s role as representing the needs of the people and not controlling the public access to information n nI want to serve our city in the best interest of our citizens and lead others by example n nI don t want to play the role of protector but rather one of a civic partner that listens and understands that we need to build an environment of prosperity that attracts people to our city from all walks of life all age groups and instills a sense of pride in living in a community that is willing to evolve to be so much more n nI believe in transparency and creating community interactions by bringing the voice of the people to city hall n nI do believe monthly in person town hall meetings are essential and necessary to keep in close touch with the public to be accessible transparent and present n nI believe that business investments that will create lasting well paid jobs are an essential basis for our city and I am concerned that several important businesses left the city during the past years We need to work on bringing good companies to our city by creating an inviting atmosphere to entice new businesses to call Palm Coast Home I would call for the creation of a committee of local business owners to identify city road blocks to a successful business atmosphere and excessive red tape and then belp devise plans to eliminate them n nWe are all facing economical challenges now more than ever following the Covid lock downs uncontrolled inflation and an uncertain economy and so is the city However I do not believe in raising taxes as the only method to create revenue to fill the city s coffers Instead I believe in creating a thriving business environment to attract investments into our city Tax revenue generated from businesses should help alleviate the pressure of tax dollars gleaned from private residential property tax As such improving the business atmosphere will bring more businesses from which the city can improve the tax base and reduce the burden on the individual n nOUR SHERIFF PARAMEDICS AND FIRE DEPARTMENTS n nSheriff nI support our county Sheriff and his deputies I believe in the work they are doing and their efforts to stem crime and remove drugs from our streets They risk their lives to bring people to justice only to have the courts let them go I have personally witnessed the Sheriff s office close a neighboring drug house and bring the perpetrators to justice n n nParamedics nI have great respect for our paramedics and fire fighting force My mother was very ill and I brought her to our home to take care of her until the end I had to call the paramedics to our home on several occasions They were always prompt courteous and gentile with her As we have an aging community the paramedics are life savers n n nFirefighters nI was here for the fires in the early s and spent a few hours out in the middle of the Pine Lakes golf course to escape the fire Then in I lost my house to the raging forest fires The firefighters did all they could to save as many homes as possible and they fought hard I use to enjoy seeing the events and comments on their Facebook page and will push to get them back online so as to help them be engaged with the community and have a direct link to present information and advertise events n n nMENTAL HEALTH nFlagler County has the dubious honor of having one of if not the highest suicide rates in Florida I experienced this first hand when my father who was diagnosed with dementia took his own life n nAlthough there was no outward sign that he was in trouble he obviously was After he passed friends and family comforted my mom for several days but she we was were then left to our own I believe there should be a city supported outreach program in Palm Coast that reaches out to families affected by these tragedies Even if it is a just a phone call with a friendly voice saying hello how is your day going n nTAXES n I have skin in the game By this I mean that I own property pay property taxes and am keenly aware of the burden increased taxes place upon the community I understand that the government is an entity that survives off of the fruits of other people s labor I will work hard to keep your taxes low and tirelessly look for areas to cut spending eliminate waste and make departments accountable I won t play games pretending a flattened milage rate is a reduction in your property taxes When property values go up the amount paid in property tax with a flat or minimally reduced milage rate still goes up Many of our residents are Senior Citizens who fled the tax drain of other states for the sunshine low taxes and a better life on their fixed incomes We have a responsibility to see to it that Seniors enjoy their retirement without the fear of high taxes and our younger generations have a chance to start without the burden of high taxation holding them back All citizens of Palm Coast deserve a responsible city government n n nA FISCALLY RESPONSIBLE GOVERNMENT nWhen your bank account gets low you tighten your belt cut out nonessential spending and revise your budget Shouldn t we expect our government to do the same thing It is beneficial for our city to receive grants from the outside but we should not be relying on outside help to soften the impact of bloated spending habits If there is waste then lets find it If there is a better way to achieve the same goals but costs less then lets do it Although we have audits that show the city is on track there are always ways to improve As we enter a time of potential reduced revenue generation for the city we should be reviewing our capital improvements with an eye for delaying or tabling projects that may not be immediately essential

Post of As promised here is the second installment from the Belleville PBA Official Endorsement Including the actual letter from the Belleville PBA and related media coverage of this historic endorsement n nThey have my back today and WILL have my back in the upcoming May election for Mayor Period n nWhy Because I ve had their back from July and whether or not I received this rare endorsement if I m blessed to serve another term as Mayor my commitment to them and to law and order would have remained steadfast n nI have not only praised them at times when it wasn t popular to do so but I also spoke out for and defended our BPD when they couldn t always do so themselves n nWhile I m proud and honored by their support I know my Father is smiling as he looks down on both me and our Belleville PD As a child I learned what public service was by watching my mom and dad My father always loved our PD and was one of the volunteers who assisted in raising money for the department s first bullet proof vests Today the plague he received from the then Commissioner is prominently displayed in the Mayor s Office n nNext I expect a letter going out from the State PBA to the hundreds of active and retired PBA Members currently living in Belleville to make them formally aware of the endorsement and strongly recommend their support n n n nIn a rare move the local police union is making an endorsement for mayor throwing its support behind Mayor Michael Melham for four more years of service n nThe endorsement posted to the Belleville PBA s official social media channels read Belleville PBA Local is proud to announce our support for Incumbent Mayor Michael Melham in his re election campaign for Mayor of the Township of Belleville Mayor Melham has time and time again shown his support for law enforcement and first responders through the Covid Pandemic as well as the sweeping anti police movement He has shown his support by standing with Local and our community n nMelham is running for re election on Tuesday May with his slate of candidates Deputy Mayor Naomy DePe a and Councilman at large Tommy Graziano n nIn receiving the endorsement Melham said he was extremely humbled and absolutely thrilled to have the support and official endorsement of the men and women of our fine Belleville Police Department n nThe endorsement is noteworthy because the Belleville PBA has not endorsed a candidate for local office in decades n n That s why Local voluntarily stepping out with its official endorsement means so much especially during these trying times Melham said This was not solicited rather it happened organically with the men and women of Local knowing I ve had their back unconditionally for years In return they wanted to show me that they have my back in this upcoming May municipal election n nThe mayor added We seem to live in a world that s upside down Good is bad and bad is somehow good These hard working men and women put their lives on the line every single day for us Sadly it has recently become all too popular to make them scapegoats often by elected officials Bureaucrats have been no better creating legislation after legislating neutering law enforcement and perpetuating a culture of disrespect This sickens to me n nMelham expressed his appreciation to Police Chief Mark Minichini as well as the PBA including PBA President John Hood and PBA Vice President State Delegate Steven Plumer n n I sincerely thank you for your strong show of support and commitment to my re election and to our collective vision of creating a BetterBelleville for all Belleville residents Melham said Stay safe and stay strong

Join us for this online discussion as part of The Open University s events for British Science Week n nFollow The Open University on Twitter and Facebook for updates on all of or BSW events nThe public understanding of genetics is fraught with oversimplifications and misconceptions This gives fertile ground for abuse by White supremacists who claim superiority via some pure ancestry or by eugenicists who assign inferiority to certain people e g with dark skin The rise of consumer level genetic tests fanned this further Both test sellers and consumers misleadingly talk about having the gene for musical ability or screening the embryo for top intelligence In this talk I will refer to my research to explain how so much of it is wishful misunderstanding and how the science is so nuanced nGet to know our expert nDr Kaustubh Adhikari is a lecturer in Statistics at The Open University He carries out research on the application of statistics to genetics after obtaining a PhD from Harvard University He has appeared on the BBC to talk about his research and on the use of statistics He does many public engagement events on the use and misuse of statistics for example about Covid

The British family farm could die out in the next years Provided British agriculture stays on the path it s on that may well be the direction we are heading According to data from Defra farms of less than hectares have halved in number in the last years Small holdings have also seen a dramatic decrease too from around in to less than in n nSmall scale family farms are facing an uncertain future putting the future of the sector at risk With increasing concerns over trade deals and the new agricultural bill looming it s an increasingly worrying time for small producers many of whom have shown incredible courage and resilience keeping the country fed through the outbreak of Covid earlier this year n nWhy are Small Scale British Farms Disappearing n nThe number of US style mega farms in the UK has increased by in the past years alone This collapse in family farms has in part been driven by the rise of concentrated animal feeding operations CAFOs In these industrial farming units pigs cows and chickens are crammed by the thousand into rows of barns Many units are semi automated with feeding run by computer with periodic visits by workers n nIndustrial farming dominates animal production and has an outsized influence on crop growing and land usage The UK is now home to at least mega farms classed as CAFOs Most highly geared industrial farms are not far off the CAFO status and there are thousands of industrial farms taking up huge swathes of British land once home to a tapestry of smaller farms n nHow Can we Create a Food System that Supports Small Scale Farms n nThere is extensive evidence of the important role that small scale farms have in our agricultural landscape creating jobs supporting rural communities and reducing inputs and waste on mixed farms n nSmall farms such as these are often written off as inefficient or low output But a study carried out by the Prince s Countryside Fund points out top performing small family farms are just as efficient as many of the country s much larger ones Especially when it comes to producing higher quality food grass fed hand reared free range self sustaining and regenerating n nSecuring a Future for Small Scale Farmers n nWe work directly with around small scale British family farms all who rear native breed meat in harmony with nature Excitingly we are also growing our range to include hundreds of products from many more small scale artisan producers around the country from small scale artisan cheesemakers to family run flour mills growing and milling heritage grains and many many more n nFor us true sustainability also includes building sustainable communities ensuring everyone in the chain is receiving a fair price and that the true cost of our food is being accounted for We aim to enable small family farms to thrive by building strong relationships direct with our customers n nBy shopping with Pipers Farm your money is going back into the community It is helping us to ensure we are able to farm in a way that tackles the climate crisis regenerating rather than depleting our soils It is funding projects such as laying down new hedgerows planting trees improving water cycles and converting to renewable energy It s allowing traditional artisan skills to thrive in rural communities providing important links such as low throughput abattoirs and local feed mills Importantly your support is securing a future for small scale British family farms n nDiscover more at

did n nHow did my opponent do See for yourself The below picture shows how Liberty Defense scored him I ll include the criteria they used to rate them here before the picture so as to eliminate any ambiguity A NO score means that that the candidate in this case my opponent failed to take advantage of amendments to make the bill as good as possible or failed to support it all together n nThis is an edit of the original post and the original advertisement I had a screenshot with the criteria in the post before but it wasn t as clear as it could be I was made aware of this by someone in my district and though I clarified in the comments I wanted to be sure that the information was very clear and easy to see n nHere are the criteria n nLife from Conception SB Amendment nThis amendment would have required the Indiana State Department of Health to revoke an entity s license if that entity knowingly and intentionally participated in ending the life of an innocent human being Indiana code already states that human life begins at conception IC SB amendment would have reinforced this definition n nProtecting Premature Babies SB Amendment nThis amendment would have protected premature babies Indiana already extends legal protections to babies who survive nabortions This amendment would ve extended these legal protections to ALL premature babies not just those who survive nabortions n nImmunity Passport Ban SB Amendment nThis amendment would have prohibited hospitals physicians offices businesses health officials or any state or local government nagency from coercing an individual to release information about their vaccination status proof of immunity or results of a medical ntest in order to participate or gather n nVaccination Status Discrimination SB Amendment nThis amendment would have ensured that employers who make c vid vaccination mandatory were not eligible for general c vid nimmunity provided by SB n nConstitutional Carry HB Amendment nThis amendment would have removed language in the Constitutional Carry bill that gun rights experts warned could lead to the creation of a Super database that would contain information about prohibited persons from NICS and IDACS Records are nnotoriously incomplete inaccurate and often times will get responses of person s with similar names Interjecting this unreliable information into a police stop that might identify an armed law abiding gun owner as a felon could create challenging situations n nRight To Worship HB Amendment nThis amendment would have protected the Right to Worship even during a state of emergency by prohibiting the Governor from nsetting limitations on church operation by executive order n nRight to Hospice Visitation HB Amendment nThis amendment would have prohibited the state a political subdivision or an officer or employee of the state or a political nsubdivision from restricting the right of an individual to visit another individual in hospice during an emergency n nRight to Nursing Home Visitation HB Amendment nThis amendment would have prohibited the state a political subdivision or an officer or employee of the state or a political nsubdivision from restricting the right of an individual to visit another individual in a nursing home during an emergency n nRight to Hospital Visitation HB Amendment nThis amendment would have prohibited the state a political subdivision or an officer or employee of the state or a political nsubdivision from restricting the right of an individual to visit another individual in a hospital during an emergency n nRight to Operate a Business HB Amendment nThis amendment would have prohibited the state a political a political subdivision or an officer or employee of the state or a npolitical subdivision from restricting the right of any business to conduct business as usual during an emergency n nRight to Gather as Families HB Amendment nThis amendment would have prohibited the state a political subdivision or an officer or employee of the state or a political nsubdivision imposing any mandates or restrictions on any individual or any family during an emergency n nParental Rights HB nThis bill allows the state In case you ve missed this n nFood Deserts Scarcity in the Land of Plenty nThe phrase food desert may sound like something from a dystopian science fiction movie but living in a food desert is a reality that a surprising number of Americans face every day The term was first coined by the Scottish Nutrition Task Force in and first introduced to the US via the Farm Bill Food Conservation and Energy Act of n nFood deserts are areas that lack access to affordable fresh meats dairy products fruits vegetables whole grains and other foods that make up a healthy diet they are a major factor in overall food insecurity in our nation The USDA defines a food desert as having a poverty rate of or greater and by how close residents are to supermarkets In urban food deserts people live more than a mile away from a supermarket In rural food deserts distance to a grocery store is greater than miles nA USDA report showed that the main characteristics of food desert areas are a very large or very sparse population low income high levels of unemployment inadequate access to transportation and a low number of food retailers providing fresh produce at affordable prices n nFood desert residents usually struggle with a combination of these factors and there are differing schools of thought regarding food deserts and their true effects n nAvailability Accessibility and Affordability Are Issues Or Are They nThe most wide spread thinking holds that residents of food deserts have difficulty juggling availability accessibility and affordability of healthy food to the extent that their health suffers Without ready access to full service supermarkets it can also be difficult for those with dietary restrictions to find appropriate food to fit their cultural or health needs n nEven in cases where healthy food is readily available the cost can be a major barrier for consumers In a comprehensive study was done that compiled data from studies in countries It showed that the cost of healthy food is about more per day than less healthy options which makes for per person per year The total increase for a family of four is over which can be a substantial amount for low income households n nIn the USDA found that million households both lived in a food desert and lacked access to a vehicle Thus the thinking goes even if those people can afford to buy healthy foods it can be difficult for them to get to a grocery store and they may therefore rely more heavily on fast food restaurants and convenience stores n nA paradox exists in urban food deserts amidst a scarcity of healthy food there is a high percentage of obese people due to the increased consumption of less healthy foods The result is a prevalence of obesity and other diet related health conditions such as diabetes and heart disease in those areas A study of Chicago neighborhoods found that deaths from diabetes in food deserts were actually double those in areas with relatively easy access to grocery stores n nConversely a study by the Journal of the American Heart Association JAHA found that association between food deserts and adverse outcomes is largely driven by low area income not poor access to food n nFurther research from New York University NYU showed between and more than a thousand supermarkets opened nationwide in neighborhoods around the country that had previously been food deserts NYU studied the grocery purchases of about households in those neighborhoods While it s true that these households buy less healthy groceries than people in wealthier neighborhoods they do not start buying healthier groceries after a new supermarket opened Instead we find that people shop at the new supermarket but they buy the same kinds of groceries they had been buying before n nIn addition the study also stated the average American travels miles to shop and percent of shopping trips are made by car In fact low income households are not much different they travel an average of miles Since we re traveling that far we tend to shop in supermarkets even if there isn t one down the street Even people who live in zip codes with no supermarkets still buy percent of their groceries from supermarkets n nConsidering that there are countless educational resources for people who wish to learn how to make good dietary choices it would seem that the biggest factor in individual health simply boils down to personal choice This is not to belittle the effects of insufficient nutrition which tends to have the heaviest effect on children in low income areas n nLong Term Effects Go Far Beyond Nutrition nNutrition or the lack thereof affects more than physical health Studies have shown that children who struggle with poor nutrition are more likely to have social and behavioral problems in school This can lead to students dropping out of school and other types of failed education which very often result in economic failures later in life n nThe long term economic cycle in areas deemed to be food deserts are vicious Multi generational families in food deserts tend to experience decreasing wealth which leads to businesses leaving the area which means fewer employment opportunities which leads to even further reduced wealth When new stores open they open in areas of higher income to reduce the risk of their investment The decreased buying power of customers in low income areas and the threat of higher crime rates whether real or perceived tend to push businesses away Some go so far as to label the results food apartheid since food insecurity affects minority groups to a greater degree n nFood Insecurity Most Prevalent in Southern States nIt follows then that the highest concentration of food insecure communities are located in areas with higher populations of minority groups n nThe USDA has calculated that there are total census tracts in the United States which fall within the parameters to be considered a food desert The USDA website states a census tract is a small relatively permanent subdivision of a county that usually contains between and people but generally averages around people Rural counties make up of total counties in the country but they make up of counties with the highest rates of food insecurity n nA December USDA survey showed that of total US households were food insecure with being at low food security status and at very low food security status These percentages account for million people including million children Of those children live in households that experience very low food security n nThis particular survey defined low food insecure households as being able to obtain enough food to mostly maintain their eating patterns or to reduce food intake by eating less varied diets This group was also able to rely on assistance from federal programs and local food pantries n nVery low food security status was defined by having the normal eating patterns of one or more household members disrupted by food scarcity and by cases of overall food intake being reduced due to lack of money and other resources to obtain food n nNo Easy Answers nConsidering the differing schools of thought on the issue is not clear how geographic location truly affects food insecurity or what measures to alleviate it are most effective n nOhio University writes Dealing with food deserts across the United States is a complex issue with no easy solutions It is difficult for communities and cities to simply build more grocery stores develop more transit options or find ways to help individuals generate more income to purchase healthy foods nConversely New York University stated Over the past decade federal and local governments in the United States have spent hundreds of millions of dollars encouraging grocery stores to open in food deserts The federal Healthy Food Financing Initiative has leveraged over billion in financing for grocers in under served areas Meanwhile cities such as Houston and Denver have sought to institute related measures at the local level n nSome mistakenly believe that subsidies for commodities like corn and soy work to lower the prices of foods that are more processed and less healthy Some blame the market driven polices that focus on turning out inexpensive high volume highly processed food products for maximum industry profit One school of thought holds that placing a sin tax on less healthy foods would discourage their purchase n nWhile a variety of programs exist to help with food insecurity they can only do so much especially considering that inflation supply chain issues and food shortages are currently impacting all Americans In fact researchers at Northwestern University found that food insecurity more than doubled because of the covid pandemic affecting up to of households Of course the already precarious situation of millions of food insecure people has been greatly exacerbated by the current state of affairs in our nation n nThrough the tangled web of issues surrounding food insecurity one thing is abundantly clear our nation s food producers are more important than ever
North Carolina patients have access to all these records and can read the reports directly Texas patients meanwhile are left in the dark

Federal Emergency Management Agency FEMA has said part of Denver s requested million reimbursement for homeless sheltering dating back to July is not eligible for reimbursement because of changes made to the city s public health orders in early n nDenver city officials estimate the portion in question could be between million and million n nFEMA provided million to Denver s congregate sheltering and non congregate sheltering operations conducted from March through June a FEMA spokesperson explained But when local public health orders changed by removing social distancing requirements for critical businesses such as emergency shelters and strongly encouraging those type of mitigation measures instead FEMA spokesman Phil Wernisch explained in an email the city s congregate sheltering practices no longer qualified for the federal program intended to help local governments n n FEMA has communicated to the city that changes to local and state Public Health Orders which no longer require social distancing along with updated FEMA policy meant that congregate sheltering costs will no longer be eligible for reimbursement n nCity officials have stressed that the federal agency is only considering a denial of the request and that a final decision hasn t been made n n We are in active negotiations with FEMA on this and continue to believe the costs are eligible for reimbursement Denver finance department communications director Julie Smith wrote in an email n nBetween million to million of the million request should qualify for reimbursement still Smith said n n We have recommended that the city separate items within the current request so costs can be clearly understood and FEMA can proceed with reimbursement for eligible expenses Wernisch explained Once an official determination has been issued the city has the right to file an appeal of the decision within days n nEven though the public health order changes predate the reimbursement made to the city through June Wernisch said FEMA does not intend to take back any of the funding already provided to the city n nWhat a denial of the reimbursement could practically mean for the city s homelessness efforts isn t clear n n We have not received a denial of federal emergency funds and thus we have not made decisions about what such a loss could mean for our programs Denver Department of Housing Stability at this address until leaving for college in After years of college I got married and over the next years lived first in the Houston area then in Floresville before getting divorced and moving to the family ranch in Three Rivers nMy mother having passed away over years ago spent the last years of her life confined to a wheelchair and on twice daily home kidney dialysis If you are not familiar with the process it is not a pleasant experience In addition to being connected to tubes for most of the day your home is transformed into a make shift hospital room and your living and dining rooms turned into storage for an unimaginable quantity of fluid boxes This is quite the burden on anyone and feeling compelled to not allow my father to shoulder that burden alone I moved back to their house nDuring the last years I spent years earning a Master s degree in Business Administration attending evening classes at the University of Texas at San Antonio I later earned a Doctorate in law being part of the inaugural class of the Evening Program for St Mary s University School of Law This whole time working full time and commuting from Three Rivers nI opened my law firm in the center of Three Rivers a decade ago Eventually I purchased the building from Michael Dubose Jeannie Snider still holds her Dance by Jeannie classes in the studio in the back of the building This can be confirmed through a search of Live Oak County Deed records and or the Tax records of the Appraisal District Twelve hour days are quite common here so a minute commute has been a blessing nIn I married Lori who has spent her career in civil service at Randolph Air Force Base and has less than years remaining until retirement Her primary residence since our marriage has been Three Rivers which can be confirmed as the address on her driver s license This has been possible since the Covid pandemic forced her agency to telework entirely from home for over a year Her office continues to telework days a week nIf you would like to visit with me in person please feel free to stop by my office at Bluhm Law Firm located at West Thornton Street Three Rivers Live Oak County Texas

nThe House unanimously passed Senate Bills and SB updates medical education accrediting provisions to ensure that Georgia is able to continue to train top caliber doctors SB requires that insurers authorize medications for chronic conditions for a minimum of one year Currently in some cases insurers require frequent reauthorization by a Georgian doctor of long term prescriptions for chronic conditions This legislation would streamline and simplify that process for patients nMilitary Men and Women to Enter Law Enforcement nSenate Bill which unanimously passed the House repays some of the costs incurred by active duty retired or honorable discharged military men and women who attend law enforcement training Costs are limited to tuition costs that are not covered by other available resources Georgia is home to one of the largest military populations in the country These men and women have served our country honorably many of them leave the military and continue to have an interest in serving their communities while having backgrounds that can transfer easily to law enforcement with additional training n nChildren in District nThe House passed Senate Bill which creates an open and transparent complaint process for parents who are concerned about harmful content in our schools n nWhile a complaint process is required now unfortunately the lack of any deadlines or required transparency means that some schools and school systems may choose to make the process more difficult than it needs to be or delay a response hoping that a complainant goes away nThis legislation simply requires that complaints be investigated in days with a parent meeting occurring within days Should a parent wish to appeal to the local school board that appeal must be heard within days nThe ultimate decision in these cases remains with schools we are simply giving parents confidence in the process n nThe House also passed Senate Bill the Unmask Georgia Students Act While most Georgia school systems have eliminated mask mandates they remain in place even today in some schools Seeing these mandates linger long past any significant perceived threat to students or teachers from Covid highlights the importance of this legislation n nSenate Bill provides that no public school board of education or school leadership can make or enforce a mask mandate without providing an opt out for parents Parents cannot be required to provide a reason and their children cannot be subject to adverse consequences for doing so n nOn a more somber note there is unfortunately evil in this world That s one of the reasons the House had to pass Senate Bill This legislation affirms that a parent found guilty of homicide in the death of his or her child cannot recover any money or property as a result of that child s death Following an emotional speech from the General Assembly s longest serving member Representative Calvin Smyre the House passed SB by a vote of n nPlease do not hesitate to call or email david jenkins house ga gov

What do you think of the state of democracy in the world today The number of countries moving in an authoritarian direction in outnumbered those going in a democratic direction Democratically elected governments including established democracies are increasingly adopting authoritarian tactics This democratic backsliding has often enjoyed significant popular support Some of the most worrying examples of backsliding are found in some of the world s largest countries Brazil and India The United States and three members of the European Union EU Hungary Poland and Slovenia have also seen concerning democratic declines Over half the countries in the world now are non democratic hybrid or authoritarian regimes n nShare your views at synthisophy com

The Calhoun County Journal has partnered with the City of Oxford to host candidate forums The forums will allow the community to learn more about the candidates and what their individual stances on current issues are The forums are open to all parties running and all candidates have been invited to participate The second scheduled forum Alabama House will be held on April in the City of Oxford at the Oxford Performing Arts Center n nThe Calhoun Journal will be submitting a list of questions to the moderators for random selection The questions will be gathered from the voting community through our website If you wish to have a question asked to the candidates please go to the Candidate Forum page and choose which forum you would like to ask a question people may ask a question for each forum All questions submitted through the website will be printed and delivered to the moderator Neither Calhoun County Journal nor the candidates will have advanced knowledge of which questions will be asked to the candidates during the forum The question form will be closed seven days prior to the event to ensure the moderator has enough time to prepare n nDuring the forum each candidate will have the opportunity to answer the same question and a possible rebuttal if one candidate addresses another candidate directly The candidate s responses will be based on a countdown timer to ensure each person has an equal opportunity to address a question n nThe forums will be open to anyone in the public that would like to attend Covid guidelines are still in effect so if community members would like to attend the event in person make sure to arrive early enough to secure a seat The Calhoun County Journal will also be live streaming the forum for those who can t attend the live event

There was an assumption that jobs such as kitchen assistants or front of house would pay minimum wage however we are currently carrying vacancies that are offering rates starting at an hour n nIt s been a tumultuous two years in Scotland s hospitality sector n nBrexit induced staff shortages have been compounded by the pandemic and subsequent lockdown restrictions n nThere were dire warnings of the collapse of a sector that directly employs around of Scotland s workforce and with another employed indirectly this means around people rely on the sector to make a living n nWhile the impact of Brexit is still playing out the announcement by the Scottish Government of an end to vaccine passports and an end to all Covid restrictions later this month means that better time lie ahead n nThe only fly in the ointment is staff shortages n nAccording to UK Hospitality Scotland there were between vacancies in the sector at the end of last year meaning up to of jobs in the industry are currently vacant n nEight out of ten businesses report vacancies in roles such as reception and waiting staff while almost have vacancies for chefs with a third reporting staff shortages for kitchen staff housekeepers and even management roles n nAll of which means that there has never been a better time to find a job in hospitality and with businesses competing in a limited pool of applicants wages which were traditionally at the lower end of the market are on a definite upward trend n nPay rates have changed significantly in recent times n nThere used to be an assumption that jobs such as kitchen assistants or front of house would pay near minimum wage however we are currently carrying vacancies that are offering rates starting at an hour by businesses throughout the Highlands and Islands n nThere is little doubt that if you choose to work in hospitality anywhere in Scotland you ve already chosen the perfect location Find all the latest hospitality vacancies on HIJOBS at

Teacher Retention and Recruitment Our excellent teachers and staff are one of our most valuable resources in education A quality teacher or staff member can make all of the difference between a successful and unsuccessful year for a student However in the last few years our teachers have been asked to do so much They had to switch to online learning at a moment s notice while dealing with technology shortages and lack of home internet This was accomplished with little to no additional training and without additional compensation for the many extra hours of work they gave in addition to their regular work hours Many gave up most of their summer without pay to help create an entirely new world in education Next teachers were tasked with providing both online and in person learning often at the same time even within one class period Our teachers and staff members were literally building the plane while flying it in the air n nThis type of task juggling pushed our teachers and staff past any boundaries they had reached before with technology and learning Simultaneously due to necessary Covid protocols students and teachers were quarantined for over a week when exposed while teaching and learning in person and that had to be factored in to lesson plans Sub shortages only complicated this matter requiring many teachers to work their off periods to cover other classes and teach classes with double the typical number of students to make sure all students had a teacher to supervise them again without additional compensation n nAll the while our teachers were barraged by the politics of Covid infection rates Covid Safety Protocols mask wearing and vaccines They were accused of not wanting to come back to work even of being lazy They were accused of being pro mask or anti mask pro vaccine or anti vaccine n nTo say the least it has been a tough few years and we are seeing record numbers of teachers leave the profession Retaining our best and brightest teachers is of critical importance One of the areas I have looked into is teacher salaries and while we as a district are above average once you have taught in our district for over years our starting salary is lower than many surrounding districts Salaries make up of our district budget I would like to look at ways that our district can be offer competitive salaries to recruit new teachers At the same time offering our existing teachers extra support like the Covid Bonus last year are things that need to be considered By balancing the needs of newer and existing teachers with competitive salaries and compensation we can excel in our goal to employ excellent educators and staff members in our district a primary need to maintain our standing as an excellent district to both work and learn in

I love talking with my friend Pat because he s full of surprising wisdom and he really helps me think things though sometimes n nOnce after a session where Pat had effortlessly given me a number of useful insights I thanked him and asked him if he had any problems or worries of his own Pat mused for a moment and then said Well if I could take even half of my own advice I d have millions of dollars and be president Or at least be able to calmly turn down the job offer n nWhy are we so bad at listening to our own wisdom sometimes n nI thought of that again when I stumbled across the text of an interview I gave a couple of years ago for another friend of mine who teaches philosophy classes The interview was from the year B C as in Before Covid It was given just before the pandemic came along to turn everything upside down Another time another age n nI felt like I d received a gift from the past And shockingly I had sent it to myself like a time capsule n nReading that interview from two years was like tuning in to a transmission from a calmer time A calmer Tim That too I was clearly in a good place B C and able to reflect More grounded more centered all the things we ve lost since the roaring s sprang on us like a famished lion on a dazed wildebeest n nI wish I would have looked back on these words a few times a day during this rough ride they might have helped reel me in a little and might have been more productive than watching The Queen s Gambit for a third time Well better late than never n nMy friend asked me this What is the purpose of a human being n nMy reply I think you can find a way to be kind A kindness for yourself and a kindness that will lead to helping others I can t think of a better purpose I think it sounds deceptively simple It s not just I ll open the car door for you I m talking about a deeper kindness to not respond to our worst reflexes To offer a genuine hand to someone based on the fact that you know that the practice of kindness will enrich I believe there s no stronger energy that can link itself to other people than the energy of kindness n nI see people who embody that and I envy them I want to be more like that and for that day and even for a week I do a pretty good job because I saw it happen and that reminds me I need more of that to bring me to a better place and space and a better way of thinking and living and doing I speak with a forked tongue because I m amazingly selfish in many ways but I try to balance that n nMy friend asked me if seeing an example of kindness and wanting to emulate it was related to education somehow n nMy answer Oh yes There are two types of educators There are educators who like to measure and there are educators who like to teach And I find that a very clear divide Kindness is not measuring Why do we want children to compete against each other and why are we measuring them I find it to be a great enemy of free thinking an enemy of kindness of mentorship of coaching I find it an enemy of love This incessant need to only measure as a way to define someone s capability that is a box a trap that is a cage around a young mind that has yet to experiment fail flourish and conquer and fail again and conquer again and that is a crime against minds That is deeply unkind n nAnother thing I talked about in the interview was not letting fear doubt and uncertainty hold you back n nAs a dyslexic and someone whose primary way of learning is through people when I was in college I still remember the Psychology class I took It was a person lecture hall and every time the teacher would say something I didn t understand I would raise my hand I raised my hand so often people booed Can you imagine being a freshman in college and being booed And you know what I kept my hand up I paid for my seat I know how I learn I got an A in that class Raise your hand and don t be afraid of the boos n nTo which I would add Also don t boo others when they re trying to learn We all learn at different paces and in different ways These are turbulent times but if we ve learned nothing else from the past two years it should be the value of patience and helping each other move forward As for me I m going to try to do more listening to others as well as to my better self

This Spring Art League will be presenting Peter Dallos Flowering a series of metal sculptures of flowers in varying stages of blooming The collection an evocative and powerful collection explores the beautiful yet sometimes spindly and bizarre forms of orchids and forest flowers n nDallos previous works explored dystopian themes such as the helplessness felt by individuals during war His previous series include Struggle and End of the Road His sculpture War series a commentary on his own experiences in Hungary during World War II and the subsequent rise of the communist regime is in the permanent collection of the Holocaust Memorial Museum in Washington DC n nFlowering was inspired during his isolation at his North Carolina cabin during the pandemic I m trying to gentle me down says Dallos Unexpectedly the full isolation during the Covid year made me tranquil Consequently I moved on from the existential worries of previous work The beauty of flowers engages me now n nDallos success as a sculptor comes after years spent as a professor of neuroscience at Northwestern University He has written an autobiography I Was Here Life Science and Art in Turbulent Times n nPeter Dallos Flowering will be on display April May An artist s reception free and open to the public will be held on Wednesday April pm

Video of Please share with your friends and family The Rutherford County Circuit Court Clerk s office continued to provide services to the community throughout the pandemic Under order from Tennessee s Supreme Court there could no longer be in person interaction with the public by government offices during the pandemic but the Clerk s office still provided needed services on a daily basis often in person but outside of the judicial building A secure metal lock box was placed outside the Judicial building allowing attorneys and citizens to drop off paperwork payments etc during regular business hours The diligent staff in the Clerk s office checked the box multiple times a day and promptly carried out their duties to ensure our legal system kept moving forward Much like restaurants that closed their dining rooms but kept their drive thru window open Melissa Harrell and her group of professionals kept the Clerk s office running and efficient The Rutherford County Clerk s office continues to lead the way in providing value through common sense reforms hard work and excellent customer service to all Rutherford County citizens rutherfordcountytn murfreesboro melissaharrellforcircuitcourtclerk

Profs and Pints DC presents Cities After Covid an examination of how the pandemic has altered the status and future of urban centers with John Rennie Short geographer scholar of urban issues and professor of public policy at the University of Maryland Baltimore County n nOne need not walk far through Washington D C to see how the pandemic has impacted different sections of the city and even businesses and people within them in very different ways Some neighborhoods have barely a trace of their former activity while others are bustling Thriving businesses stand next to boarded storefronts Office buildings remain mostly empty and parts of town feel more dangerous The housing market is in a huge period of flux n nAre our nation s cities going to return to the way they were If not what will the post pandemic city look like n nCome hear such questions tackled by Dr John Rennie Short a geographer who has extensively monitored and written about the changes that cities have undergone since Covid first hit here in the late winter of He ll give an overview of what we know looking at population shifts and how differences in U S and European approaches to pandemic relief had markedly different impacts on cities He ll examine the health of downtown businesses and look at crime trends and their impact n nLooking forward he ll discuss how cities are likely to be altered by more people working from home companies settling into hybrid work weeks and consumers greater reliance on online shopping He ll also discuss the role played by the distinct characteristics of specific cities and whether cities with a substantial creative class are likely to bounce back better than others n nThe obituary of the American cities has been written before both the invention of the telephone and the terrorist attacks led some to declare them doomed Will they recover this time enough to someday regard the pandemic as temporary setback Advance tickets Doors save with a student ID HIPAA the acronym for the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act has come up a lot since the beginning of the COVID pandemic You may have seen people on social media or news shows discussing their HIPAA rights regarding masks or vaccinations In short HIPAA is a federal law that protects patients sensitive health information from being disclosed without their knowledge or consent

Broadband Internet nA topic that is hurled out there every election cycle is what are you going to do to bring jobs to this county The question seems to have been dwarfed this cycle by flooding and traffic congestion however here s a thought n nOur Federal Government has gone off the deep end with making inadequate and irresponsible legislation making us conservatives nervous as to what the future will hold The cost of living is rising faster than our wages People are scrambling to find ways to save their wages in order to keep up with inflation n nOf all the programs that are on the horizon to be forced upon us one may be useful n nI am speaking of broadband internet service As we went through COVID we saw a great swing to work from home opportunities I have been speaking with people who are happy about working from home and enjoying benefits such as spending more time with family saving money by curbing commuting expenses and raises they have achieved by working jobs that are outside the county and sometimes out of state jobs that were otherwise unavailable due to physical location This could be the solution to our families concerns Those concerns being their children are leaving and not returning because there are too few well paying jobs n nBroadband internet would also benefit rural college students whose parents are making sacrifices to ensure their children can excel in a competitive job market Because most classes and supporting software run off highspeed internet these students are having to drive to locations with faster internet sources to study such as Starbucks Panera Bread or Whataburger n nBroadband will also open doors by allowing uninterrupted video class meets and faster material uploads for online schools certifications or accreditations in a number of fields which can lead to advancement in a current job or better jobs in fields they are passionate about I know this personally n nCurrently rural businesses within our county are struggling with the lack of dependable internet connectivity Examples of these struggles include the inability to run a debit credit card machine at our local rural businesses and cell phone hotspots that are not reliable enough for a debit credit card machine either Losing connections can delay invoicing ordering and causes miscommunication which is detrimental to independent businesses located throughout our beautiful county n nAnother sector affected by unreliable internet connectivity is home based employees An example is those who work for Navy Federal one of the area s largest employers of at home based employees that pays above average wages Employees have expressed the fear and frustration of always having to explain to Navy Federal that the internet was awful and unreliable while praying daily that Navy Federal continues to have patience with them Based on my observation of the housing market climbing so rapidly over the last two years I do not believe that the solution is sell out and move into town after all there are no houses in town to move to n nWith the addition of broadband not only could it make stable these examples and more like them but it could also lead to a more technical workforce living and spending their income here in our county Possibly a much better scenario is it promotes families to live in a slower country setting allowing them to focus more on the family and find the joy we already know n nDuring my trip to Greenville SC a friend was showing me how their community took its abandoned textile factories and rundown buildings to re invent the city s town life Local investors using their money invested in their town and attracted a younger tech driven crowd This crowd successfully changed and bred new life into a gloomy depressed part of town n nWith the state jockeying a position to receive million dollars or more this seems to have some promise in making some positive influences in our beloved county This is just something to work towards with the help of us all

Research suggests that the rates of elder abuse in the United States have nearly doubled during the pandemic affecting one in five older persons writes Allie Yang Green senior manager at Equal Justice Works A public health crisis and a human rights issue elder abuse is one of the most prevalent forms of abuse in the country and it has only worsened since the onset of the COVID pandemic n nIn observance of National Crime Victims Rights Week we re sharing stories of how our Elder Justice Program Fellows have advocated for abuse victims in predominantly rural communities throughout the country Since Fellows have assisted close to older adults helping to address unmet legal needs stemming from abuse Combining direct legal services with extensive education and outreach activities in their communities Fellows in the Elder Justice Program are helping to improve the national response to elder abuse and create a society where all people regardless of age can live with dignity and security n nHear from Fellows Caitlin Corey hosted by Northwest Texas Legal Assistance and Benjamin Taylor hosted by Legal Aid Society of Louisville in a new blog on our website

Campaign funding tallies in tens of thousands nBy Mitchell Kirk Daily R eportermkirk greenfieldreporter com nApril n nHANCOCK COUNTY Tens of thousands of dollars are backing campaigns in the upcoming primary election including from residents candidates themselves and companies doing business with county government n nReports due earlier this month document campaigns contributions and expenditures dating back to the beginning of the year n nMarc Huber a Republican seeking reelection for his Hancock County Board of Commissioners District seat came into the reporting period with nearly and tallied nearly more in contributions n nHuber who s running for a third term on the board of commissioners said his campaign had a couple fundraisers in preparation for next week s election n n That s usually what we ve always done in the past he said We ve had some corporate people invest in our campaign and we ve had local people invest in it as well n nAmong those corporate contributors are companies and executives of companies with speculative warehouse developments in western Hancock County including from Columbia South Carolina based Red Rock Developments and each from Carmel based Lauth John Bumgarner of Cincinnati based Al Neyer and Ryan Gallmeyer of Indianapolis based Ambrose Property Group n nHuber has supported much of the speculative warehouse development in the western part of the county but not all He voted against the creation of a special taxing district last year to facilitate a Red Rock Developments project citing a lack of assurances that it would benefit public safety and schools The commissioners have since adopted a practice of entering into economic development agreements with warehouse developers that outline tax breaks as well as payments for operational public safety and school purposes n nLaw firms and lawyers involved in the western developments have contributed to Huber s campaign as well including from Matthew Price of Dentons Indianapolis office and another from an investment company he runs from Barnes Thornburg s Indianapolis office and from Briane House of Greenfield based Pritzke Davis n nDustin Frye of Fishers based RQAW which is leading construction on the county s soon to open new jail contributed to Huber s campaign n n It s not that uncommon Huber said If you look at anybody s campaign financing people that work for the county and do things for the county they tend to contribute It s not a payoff n nIndiana Rep Chris Jeter R Fishers whose district includes part of northwestern Hancock County contributed to Huber s campaign as well n nGary McDaniel a Republican Greenfield City Council member looking to replace Huber came into the reporting period with nearly and raised another His backers include fellow city council members George Plisinski and Mitch Pendlum as well as Ray Richardson who served as county attorney for years before the board of commissioners replaced him in n nDavid Clapper and Sandra Hudson western county residents and outspoken critics of the development there also supported McDaniel n nMcDaniel has been critical of that development as well arguing that the infrastructure in that area is lacking for such large complexes n n It s unbelievable that we can go at something this unprepared he said I hope to work with the other commissioners and we can step back for a minute and see what we can do to make the lives of the taxpayers better n nMore focus needs to be placed on residential development in the western part of the county McDaniel said n nMuch of Republican incumbent Hancock County Prosecutor Brent Eaton s campaign coffers consists of a loan of over from himself He said he started setting money aside more than a year ago n n Had to tighten the belt a little bit around the house and that s just the way it is Eaton said n nHe noted COVID risks that persisted through the winter made it challenging to hold fundraising events n n It was very difficult to have the type of in person events which have been the lifeblood of campaign fundraising in the past he said n nGrey Chandler a Republican looking to replace Eaton reported over in contributions much of which from family and himself He also reported a loan from himself to his campaign n n I like the idea that I don t owe anybody any favors he said I m not saying other candidates who fund raise would feel that way but I think it s a lot easier when there s no issues like that I certainly accepted donations from those who reached out and wanted to give but I didn t make serious fundraising efforts n nChandler a former Madison County deputy prosecutor added he s reached out to lawyers he s had good relationships with in the past for donations but has yet to hear back n nAlong with candidates seeking office a public question is also on the ballot for voters in the Mt Vernon Community School Corporation district regarding a new property tax of up to cents per of assessed value from through as late as School officials say the tax is needed as a decade long funding boost allowed by the state draws to a close and as property tax caps continue to limit revenue available to schools It comes as the school corporation embarks on an expansion to keep up with its projected student population growth that includes building a new elementary school n nA committee advocating for the tax increase has raised over for its campaign including from Mt Vernon staff and school board members as well as from the Indiana Kentucky Ohio Regional Council of Carpenters n nMike McCarty a former Mt Vernon school board member and co chair of the Mt Vernon Community Growing Stronger Together committee said even more important than raising funds for the committee has been raising awareness about the needs for the tax increase throughout the school district Chief among those needs he continued is maintaining competitive pay for teachers to ensure the school corporation doesn t lose them and making sure class sizes don t get too big n n Schools are the centers of our communities McCarty said n nAttempts to reach the Indiana Kentucky Ohio Regional Council of Carpenters for comment were unsuccessful McCarty did not want to speak on their behalf but said he s grateful for the group s support n n They re part of the community somehow and feel very strongly obviously he said n nBill Bolander the incumbent Republican Hancock County Council member representing District in the southwestern part of the county reported a sole campaign contribution consisting of a loan from himself n n I ve always funded it myself pretty much said Bolander who s in his sixth term on the council n nBolander added he received a contribution from the Metropolitan Indianapolis Board of Realtors but that it s yet to be deposited He thinks that support stems from his advocacy for higher residential design standards as the council s representative on the Hancock County Area Plan Commission n nScott Wooldridge a Republican looking to replace Bolander came into the reporting period with nearly and raised another n nAlong with McDaniel s campaign Clapper also contributed to Wooldridge s Wooldridge has been critical of the development surge in the western part of the county as well The county council can influence that development via tax abatements something Wooldridge feels Bolander and other council members have been too generous on Wooldridge thinks abatements could be scrutinized more and last shorter durations n n We need to do the people s work and not just our own agendas he said n nClapper a commercial real estate analyst said he supports McDaniel because of his desire to pause on industrial development and think more about residential development and supports Wooldridge because of his promise to put constituents feelings over his own n n I m not against development but it s got to be development that makes sense Clapper said n nJeannine Gray the incumbent Republican Hancock County Council member representing council District came into the reporting period with over and raised another Her opponent Scott Ruble reported an in kind contribution of over to his campaign from his business Ruble Outdoor Concepts Inc

offices closed or reduced onsite staff office hours and services due to the COVID pandemic An internal audit requested by me in January revealed major procedural deficiencies within the areas evaluated Thousands of case files had to digitized and destroyed per a change to the rules of recordkeeping criminal expunctions were issued by our District Attorney and processed by our clerk s office within months The State of North Carolina processes about expunctions per year for all NC counties I managed significant policy changes as our state administrative office leadership transitioned from former Chief Justice Cheri Beasley dem to Chief Justice Paul Newby rep and as our local district court leadership transitioned from former Chief District Court Judge Lisa Menefee dem to Chief District Court Judge Victoria Roemer rep And I had to run for re election months after assuming office n nEarly voting starts tomorrow Vote to keep me DENISE HINES as your Forsyth County skill and confidence to successfully navigate the challenges of this abbreviated year term of office I m seeking one more term as your Forsyth County Clerk of Superior Court During my next term I want
